DE   RecName: Full=Frizzled-3;
DE            Short=Fz-3;
DE            Short=Xfz3;
DE   Flags: Precursor;
GN   Name=fzd3; Synonyms=fz3;
OS   Xenopus laevis (African clawed frog).
OC   Eukaryota; Metazoa; Chordata; Craniata; Vertebrata; Euteleostomi;
OC   Amphibia; Batrachia; Anura; Pipoidea; Pipidae; Xenopodinae; Xenopus;

RP   NUCLEOTIDE SEQUENCE [MRNA].
RC   TISSUE=Embryo;
RX   PubMed=9510023; DOI=10.1016/S0925-4773(97)00166-4;
RA   Shi D.-L., Goisset C., Boucaut J.-C.;
RT   "Expression of Xfz3, a Xenopus frizzled family member, is restricted
RT   to the early nervous system.";
RL   Mech. Dev. 70:35-47(1998).
RN   [2]
RP   MUTAGENESIS, DOMAIN K-T-X-X-X-W MOTIF, AND COUPLING TO BETA-CATENIN
RP   PATHWAY.
RX   PubMed=10990458; DOI=10.1093/emboj/19.18.4944;
RA   Umbhauer M., Djiane A., Goisset C., Penzo-Mendez A., Riou J.-F.,
RA   Boucaut J.-C., Shi D.-L.;
RT   "The C-terminal cytoplasmic Lys-Thr-X-X-X-Trp motif in frizzled
RT   receptors mediates Wnt/beta-catenin signalling.";
RL   EMBO J. 19:4944-4954(2000).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway, which
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. Activated by Wnt8.
CC       Involved in transduction and intercellular transmission of
CC       polarity information during tissue morphogenesis and/or in
CC       differentiated tissues. Plays a role in controlling early axon
CC       growth and guidance processes necessary for the formation of a
CC       subset of central and peripheral major fiber tracts. Involved in
CC       the migration of cranial neural crest cells. May also be
CC       implicated in the transmission of sensory information from the
CC       trunk and limbs to the brain. Controls commissural sensory axons
CC       guidance after midline crossing along the anterior-posterior axis
CC       in the developing spinal cord in a Wnt-dependent signaling
CC       pathway. Together with FZD6, is involved in the neural tube
CC       closure and plays a role in the regulation of the establishment of
CC       planar cell polarity (PCP). Promotes neurogenesis by maintaining
CC       sympathetic neuroblasts within the cell cycle in a beta-catenin-
CC       dependent manner (By similarity). {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q61086}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein. Cell
CC       membrane {ECO:0000305}; Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000305}.
CC       Cell surface {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q61086}. Apical cell membrane
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q61086}; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expression restricted to the early nervous
CC       system.
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: Low expression from cleavage stages to the
CC       end of gastrulation; increases from neurulation onward. During
CC       neurulation, first localized to the anterior neural folds. As
CC       neurulation proceeds, the expression extends to the trunk neural
CC       fold, with low levels in the posterior neural fold. At the end of
CC       neurulation, strongly expressed as a large band in the midbrain.
CC       After neural tube closure, also detected in the optic lobes and
CC       otic vesicles. During the late development, expression remains
CC       restricted to the nervous system. Detected until at least the
CC       larval stages.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Lys-Thr-X-X-X-Trp motif interacts with the PDZ domain of
CC       Dvl (Disheveled) family members and is involved in the activation
CC       of the Wnt/beta-catenin signaling pathway.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10990458}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The FZ domain is involved in binding with Wnt ligands.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

RP   NUCLEOTIDE SEQUENCE [MRNA] OF 307-592.
RX   PubMed=10781956; DOI=10.1016/S0925-4773(00)00263-X;
RA   Stark M.R., Biggs J.J., Schoenwolf G.C., Rao M.S.;
RT   "Characterization of avian frizzled genes in cranial placode
RT   development.";
RL   Mech. Dev. 93:195-200(2000).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway, which
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. May be involved in
CC       transduction and intercellular transmission of polarity
CC       information during tissue morphogenesis and/or in differentiated
CC       tissues.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein. Cell
CC       membrane {ECO:0000250}; Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in the lens, otic placode (medial
CC       wall of the vesicle) and in epibranchial placode. Also expressed
CC       in the developing somites (dermomyotome).
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: Somites and placodal expression appears at
CC       stage 9. At this stage, more obvious expression is detected in the
CC       neural tube (midbrain and rostral hindbrain), and persists through
CC       about stage 15. Strongly expressed in the ectoderm and around the
CC       otic placodes at stage 12. At stage 16, otic expression declines,
CC       expression in epibranchial placodes begins and peaks at stage 20.
CC       Expression in the lens of the eye is first seen at about stage 15,
CC       more evident at stage 16. At stage 17, seen in the ectoderm and
CC       mesenchyme of the limb primordia. Detected at stage 20 in the lip
CC       of the optic cup, in the mesenchyme surrounding the eye, in the
CC       ectoderm overlying the lens and in the ectoderm caudal and ventral
CC       of the olfactory placodes. From stages 20-30, expressed in
CC       cartilage and in the dermomyotomes and migrating sclerotomal cells
CC       forming vertebrae.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Lys-Thr-X-X-X-Trp motif interacts with the PDZ domain of
CC       Dvl (Disheveled) family members and is involved in the activation
CC       of the Wnt/beta-catenin signaling pathway. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The FZ domain is involved in binding with Wnt ligands.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway, which
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. May be involved in
CC       transduction and intercellular transmission of polarity
CC       information during tissue morphogenesis and/or in differentiated
CC       tissues. Together with FZD3, is involved in the neural tube
CC       closure and plays a role in the regulation of the establishment of
CC       planar cell polarity (PCP), particularly in the orientation of
CC       asymmetric bundles of stereocilia on the apical faces of a subset
CC       of auditory and vestibular sensory cells located in the inner ear
CC       (By similarity). {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q61089}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       Q8N474:SFRP1; NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-8754490, EBI-3940687;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q61089};
CC       Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000255}. Cell membrane
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q61089}; Multi-pass membrane protein
CC       {ECO:0000255}. Cell surface {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q61089}. Apical
CC       cell membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000255}.
CC       Cytoplasmic vesicle membrane {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q61089};
CC       Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000255}. Note=Colocalizes with
CC       FZD3 at the apical face of cells (By similarity).
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q61089}.
CC   -!- ALTERNATIVE PRODUCTS:
CC       Event=Alternative splicing; Named isoforms=2;
CC       Name=1;
CC         IsoId=O60353-1; Sequence=Displayed;
CC       Name=2;
CC         IsoId=O60353-2; Sequence=VSP_044291;
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Detected in adult heart, brain, placenta,
CC       lung, liver, skeletal muscle, kidney, pancreas, thymus, prostate,
CC       testis, ovary, small intestine and colon. In the fetus, expressed
CC       in brain, lung, liver and kidney.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Lys-Thr-X-X-X-Trp motif interacts with the PDZ domain of
CC       Dvl (Disheveled) family members and is involved in the activation
CC       of the Wnt/beta-catenin signaling pathway. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The FZ domain is involved in binding with Wnt ligands.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- PTM: Ubiquitinated by ZNRF3, leading to its degradation by the
CC       proteasome. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DISEASE: Nail disorder, non-syndromic congenital, 10 (NDNC10)
CC       [MIM:614157]: A nail disorder characterized by a variable degree
CC       of onychauxis (thick nails), hyponychia, and onycholysis of all
CC       nails, with claw-shaped fingernails in some individuals. No other
CC       anomalies of ectodermal tissues, including hair, teeth, sweat
CC       glands, or skin, are noted, and individuals with dysplastic nails
CC       have normal hearing and normal psychomotor development.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:21665003}. Note=The disease is caused by
CC       mutations affecting the gene represented in this entry.
CC   -!- DISEASE: Note=Rare non-synonymous variants in FZD6 may contribute
CC       to neural tube defects, congenital malformations of the central
CC       nervous system and adjacent structures related to defective neural
CC       tube closure during the first trimester of pregnancy.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

RL   Nat. Commun. 7:12101-12101(2016).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway, which
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. May be involved in
CC       transduction and intercellular transmission of polarity
CC       information during tissue morphogenesis and/or in differentiated
CC       tissues.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Interacts with MAGI3 and DVL1 (By similarity). Interacts
CC       with MYOC. Binds to SDCBP; this interaction is increased by
CC       inositol trisphosphate (IP3) (PubMed:27386966). {ECO:0000250,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:19188438, ECO:0000269|PubMed:27386966}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       O00560:SDCBP; NbExp=4; IntAct=EBI-746917, EBI-727004;
CC       Q9UMX0:UBQLN1; NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-746917, EBI-741480;
CC       P56703:WNT3; NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-746917, EBI-3644922;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:27386966};
CC       Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000269|PubMed:27386966}.
CC       Endosome membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:27386966}; Multi-pass
CC       membrane protein {ECO:0000269|PubMed:27386966}. Note=Associated to
CC       the plasma membrane in the presence of FZD7 and
CC       phosphatidylinositol 4,5-bisphosphate (PIP2). Localized in
CC       recycling endosomes in other conditions.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:27386966}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: High expression in adult skeletal muscle and
CC       fetal kidney, followed by fetal lung, adult heart, brain, and
CC       placenta. Specifically expressed in squamous cell esophageal
CC       carcinomas.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Lys-Thr-X-X-X-Trp motif interacts with the PDZ domain of
CC       Dvl (Disheveled) family members and is involved in the activation
CC       of the Wnt/beta-catenin signaling pathway. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The FZ domain is involved in binding with Wnt ligands.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- PTM: Ubiquitinated by ZNRF3, leading to its degradation by the
CC       proteasome. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

RA   Stapleton M., Brokstein P., Hong L., Agbayani A., Carlson J.W.,

RL   Submitted (DEC-2003) to the EMBL/GenBank/DDBJ databases.
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway, which
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. Required to coordinate
CC       the cytoskeletons of epidermal cells to produce a parallel array
CC       of cuticular hairs and bristles. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10498678,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:10704878}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane {ECO:0000305}; Multi-pass membrane
CC       protein {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Wing, leg and eye imaginal disks. In embryos,
CC       expressed is seen in brain, proventriculus, Malpighian tubules,
CC       anal plate and visceral mesoderm of parasegment 8.
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: Expressed in embryos from stage 11 and in
CC       larvae.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The FZ domain is involved in binding with Wnt ligands.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

RP   INTERACTION WITH LYPD6.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway, which
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. May be involved in
CC       transduction and intercellular transmission of polarity
CC       information during tissue morphogenesis and/or in differentiated
CC       tissues. Activation by Wnt8, Wnt5A or Wnt3A induces expression of
CC       beta-catenin target genes. Displays an axis-inducing activity.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10097073}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Interacts with lypd6 and the interaction is strongly
CC       enhanced by wnt3a (PubMed:23987510).
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:23987510}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       Q6EHH9:FRIED; NbExp=2; IntAct=EBI-7735236, EBI-7735259;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10097073};
CC       Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10097073}. Cell
CC       membrane {ECO:0000250}; Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: First expressed at high levels in the late
CC       blastula stages. At early gastrula, expressed in the deep cells of
CC       the Spemann organizer prior to involution of the dorsal blastopore
CC       lip. Detected in presumptive neurectoderm as gastrulation
CC       proceeds. Becomes restricted to the anterior ectoderm by the end
CC       of gastrulation. At neurula stages, localized in the most anterior
CC       region of the embryo, mainly in the anterior ectoderm including
CC       telencephalic and cement gland regions.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Lys-Thr-X-X-X-Trp motif interacts with the PDZ domain of
CC       Dvl (Disheveled) family members and is involved in the activation
CC       of the Wnt/beta-catenin signaling pathway. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The FZ domain is involved in binding with Wnt ligands.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway, which
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. Required to coordinate
CC       the cytoskeletons of epidermal cells to produce a parallel array
CC       of cuticular hairs and bristles.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: G protein-coupled receptor that probably associates with
CC       the patched protein (PTCH) to transduce the hedgehog's proteins
CC       signal. Binding of sonic hedgehog (SHH) to its receptor patched is
CC       thought to prevent normal inhibition by patched of smoothened
CC       (SMO) (By similarity). Required for the accumulation of KIF7, GLI2
CC       and GLI3 in the cilia. Interacts with DLG5 at the ciliary base to
CC       induce the accumulation of KIF7 and GLI2 at the ciliary tip for
CC       GLI2 activation (PubMed:25644602). {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q99835,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:25644602}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homodimer (By similarity). Interacts with ARRB2
CC       (PubMed:15618519). Interacts with BBS5 and BBS7; the interactions
CC       are indicative for the association of SMO with the BBsome complex
CC       to facilitate ciliary localization of SMO (PubMed:22072986).
CC       Interacts with KIF7, DLG5 and SDCBP (PubMed:25644602).
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q99835, ECO:0000269|PubMed:15618519,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:22072986, ECO:0000269|PubMed:25644602}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein. Cell
CC       projection, cilium {ECO:0000269|PubMed:25644602}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

DE            Short=Fz-5;

OC   Eukaryota; Metazoa; Chordata; Craniata; Vertebrata; Euteleostomi;
OC   Amphibia; Batrachia; Anura; Pipoidea; Pipidae; Xenopodinae; Xenopus;

RP   NUCLEOTIDE SEQUENCE [MRNA].
RX   PubMed=11335120; DOI=10.1016/S0925-4773(01)00327-6;
RA   Sumanas S., Ekker S.C.;
RT   "Xenopus frizzled-5: a frizzled family member expressed exclusively in
RT   the neural retina of the developing eye.";
RL   Mech. Dev. 103:133-136(2001).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway, which
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. May be involved in
CC       transduction and intercellular transmission of polarity
CC       information during tissue morphogenesis and/or in differentiated
CC       tissues.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein. Cell
CC       membrane {ECO:0000250}; Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in retina.
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: First detected at the late neurula stage in
CC       retinal primordia. Throughout the tailbud stage, expressed
CC       exclusively in the neural retina within the optic vesicles. During
CC       tadpole stage, expression becomes restricted to the ciliary
CC       marginal zone.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Lys-Thr-X-X-X-Trp motif interacts with the PDZ domain of
CC       Dvl (Disheveled) family members and is involved in the activation
CC       of the Wnt/beta-catenin signaling pathway. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The FZ domain is involved in binding with Wnt ligands.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

RP   FUNCTION, AND DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE.
RX   PubMed=25639794; DOI=10.1016/j.chom.2014.12.012;
RA   Lee K.A., Kim B., Bhin J., Kim D.H., You H., Kim E.K., Kim S.H.,
RA   Ryu J.H., Hwang D., Lee W.J.;
RT   "Bacterial uracil modulates Drosophila DUOX-dependent gut immunity via
RT   Hedgehog-induced signaling endosomes.";
RL   Cell Host Microbe 17:191-204(2015).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Segment polarity protein required for correct patterning
CC       of every segment. G protein-coupled receptor that associates with
CC       the patched protein (ptc) to transduce the hedgehog (hh) signal
CC       through the activation of an inhibitory G-protein. In the absence
CC       of hh, ptc represses the constitutive signaling activity of smo
CC       through fused (fu). Essential component of a hh-signaling pathway
CC       which regulates the Duox-dependent gut immune response to
CC       bacterial uracil; required to activate Cad99C-dependent endosome
CC       formation, norpA-dependent Ca2+ mobilization and p38 MAPK, which
CC       are essential steps in the Duox-dependent production of reactive
CC       oxygen species (ROS) in response to intestinal bacterial infection
CC       (PubMed:25639794).
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Interacts with cos. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15691767}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       O16844:cos; NbExp=5; IntAct=EBI-142245, EBI-102069;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15616566};
CC       Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000255}.
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: Expressed at all developmental stages, though
CC       the levels vary.
CC   -!- PTM: Phosphorylation by CkIalpha and PKA regulates smo
CC       accumulation at the cell surface and its signaling activity in
CC       response to hh. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15616566}.
CC   -!- DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE: RNAi-mediated knockdown severely reduces
CC       adult survival following the ingestion of E.carotovora. Abolishes
CC       Cad99C-dependent formation of endosomes and DUOX-dependent up-
CC       regulation of reactive oxygen species (ROS) in the intestines of
CC       adults fed bacteria-derived uracil. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:25639794}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- CAUTION: It is uncertain whether Met-1, Met-9, Met-13 or Met-14 is
CC       the initiator. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway, which
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. May be involved in
CC       transduction and intercellular transmission of polarity
CC       information during tissue morphogenesis and/or in differentiated
CC       tissues.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       P39688:Fyn (xeno); NbExp=4; IntAct=EBI-6254477, EBI-524514;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein. Cell
CC       membrane {ECO:0000250}; Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Widely expressed. In the adult, mainly found
CC       in heart, placenta, skeletal muscle, lung, kidney, pancreas,
CC       prostate, testis, ovary and colon. In the fetus, expressed in
CC       brain, lung and kidney. Low levels in fetal liver.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Lys-Thr-X-X-X-Trp motif interacts with the PDZ domain of
CC       Dvl (Disheveled) family members and is involved in the activation
CC       of the Wnt/beta-catenin signaling pathway. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The FZ domain is involved in binding with Wnt ligands.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- PTM: Ubiquitinated by ZNRF3, leading to its degradation by the
CC       proteasome. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

RP   FUNCTION, DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE, AND CONDITIONAL KNOCKOUTS.
RX   PubMed=24799694; DOI=10.1073/pnas.1406399111;
RA   Hua Z.L., Jeon S., Caterina M.J., Nathans J.;

RT   the mouse central nervous system.";
RL   Proc. Natl. Acad. Sci. U.S.A. 111:E3005-E3005(2014).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway, which
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. Activation by Wnt5A
CC       stimulates PKC activity via a G-protein-dependent mechanism.
CC       Involved in transduction and intercellular transmission of
CC       polarity information during tissue morphogenesis and/or in
CC       differentiated tissues. Plays a role in controlling early axon
CC       growth and guidance processes necessary for the formation of a
CC       subset of central and peripheral major fiber tracts. Required for
CC       the development of major fiber tracts in the central nervous
CC       system, including: the anterior commissure, the corpus callosum,
CC       the thalamocortical, corticothalamic and nigrostriatal tracts, the
CC       corticospinal tract, the fasciculus retroflexus, the
CC       mammillothalamic tract, the medial lemniscus, and ascending fiber
CC       tracts from the spinal cord to the brain. In the peripheral
CC       nervous system, controls axon growth in distinct populations of
CC       cranial and spinal motor neurons, including the facial
CC       branchimotor nerve, the hypoglossal nerve, the phrenic nerve, and
CC       motor nerves innervating dorsal limbs. Involved in the migration
CC       of cranial neural crest cells. May also be implicated in the
CC       transmission of sensory information from the trunk and limbs to
CC       the brain. Controls commissural sensory axons guidance after
CC       midline crossing along the anterior-posterior axis in the
CC       developing spinal cord in a Wnt-dependent signaling pathway.
CC       Together with FZD6, is involved in the neural tube closure and
CC       plays a role in the regulation of the establishment of planar cell
CC       polarity (PCP), particularly in the orientation of asymmetric
CC       bundles of stereocilia on the apical faces of a subset of auditory
CC       and vestibular sensory cells located in the inner ear. Promotes
CC       neurogenesis by maintaining sympathetic neuroblasts within the
CC       cell cycle in a beta-catenin-dependent manner.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12351730, ECO:0000269|PubMed:14671310,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:16407530, ECO:0000269|PubMed:16495441,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:21325504, ECO:0000269|PubMed:24347548,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:24799694}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Interacts with VANGL2. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16687519}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein. Cell
CC       membrane {ECO:0000250}; Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000250}.
CC       Cell surface {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16495441}. Apical cell membrane
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16495441}; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC       Note=Colocalizes with FZD6 at the apical face of the cell.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16495441}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in the cortex, diencephalon, rostral
CC       brainstem and little or no staining is seen in the striatum or
CC       cerebellum. Expressed in both hair cells and supporting cells in
CC       the utricle, saccule, cristae and the organ of Corti in the inner
CC       ear (at protein level). Highly expressed in the CNS. In skin, it
CC       is restricted to the epidermis and to the developing hair
CC       follicle. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11407985,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:12351730, ECO:0000269|PubMed:16495441,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:8626800}.
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: Expressed throughout the developing central
CC       nervous system (CNS). Expressed in the cortex, diencephalon, and
CC       brainstem, with the most intense staining in the striatum and
CC       trigeminal ganglia at 18 dpc (at protein level). First detected in
CC       discrete foci in the developing epidermis of 13 days old embryos,
CC       later in the hair follicle placodes of 15 days old embryos.
CC       Expressed in the ventral and lateral margins of the spinal cord
CC       from 9.5 to 13.5 dpc, where post-crossing commissural axons
CC       project longitudinally. Expressed in superior sympathetic cervical
CC       ganglia (SCG) at 14.5 and 16.5 dpc, a stage when the SCG is
CC       comprised primarily of proliferating sympathetic neuroblasts. In
CC       17 days embryos and 1 day old newborn, expression is limited to
CC       suprabasal keratinocytes and is not seen in pelage follicles until
CC       3 days postpartum. In 7 days old neonatal skin, expression occurs
CC       throughout the epidermis and in the outer cell layers of hair
CC       follicles. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11407985,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:12351730, ECO:0000269|PubMed:14671310,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:21325504}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Lys-Thr-X-X-X-Trp motif interacts with the PDZ domain of
CC       Dvl (Disheveled) family members and is involved in the activation
CC       of the Wnt/beta-catenin signaling pathway. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The FZ domain is involved in binding with Wnt ligands.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- PTM: Ubiquitinated by ZNRF3, leading to its degradation by the
CC       proteasome. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE: Neonate knockout mice have a curly tail,
CC       flexed lower limbs, breathe irregularly and typically die within
CC       30 min of birth. Central nervous system (CNS) shows severe defects
CC       in the development of several major axon tracts, including: a
CC       nearly complete absence of the three early most prominent axon
CC       tracts in the brain and the ventral branch of the trigeminal
CC       nerve, absence of subcortical and striatal axons, the anterior
CC       commissure, misrouting of thalamocortical axons, a nearly complete
CC       absence of the corticospinal tract, the fasciculus retroflexus,
CC       and the mammillothalamic tract, poor fasciculation of the medial
CC       lemniscus and a disorganization of axon bundles in the reticular
CC       formation, severe defect in the asymmetric rostrocaudal
CC       orientation of dopaminergic and serotonergic axons, a large
CC       reduction or complete absence of ascending spinal axon tracts in
CC       the braistem, midbrain and thalamus, peripheral nerves defect in
CC       several motor neurons, such as in the VIIth and XIIth cranial
CC       motor nerves, the phrenic nerve, and the spinal motor nerve which
CC       failed to form connections with their respective targets and
CC       display also aberrant migration of a subpopulation of cranial
CC       neural crest cells (PubMed:12351730, PubMed:24347548,
CC       PubMed:24799694). Neonate knockout mice show fewer S-phase
CC       proliferating neuroblasts, premature cell cycle exit and enhanced
CC       apoptosis in early-stage superior cervical ganglia (SCGs), and in
CC       some cases, complete absence of sympathetic innervation of several
CC       peripheral targets (PubMed:21325504). Display also impaired
CC       rostral turning by growth cones of spinal cord commissural sensory
CC       axons (PubMed:14671310). FZD3 and FZD6 double knockout embryos
CC       have a curled tail, exhibit defects in neural tube and eyelids
CC       closure, in the orientation of hair bundles on inner-ear sensory
CC       cells and die at birth (PubMed:16495441). The following
CC       conditional knockout mice display the corresponding phenotypes:
CC       dopaminergic neuron-specific shows a defect in the orientation and
CC       growth of midbrain dopaminergic axons with an absence of striatum
CC       innervation; retinal ganglion cell (RGC)-specific displays a
CC       misrouting of a subset of optic tract axons and a lack of the
CC       medial terminal nucleus (MTN) innervation; neocortex neuron-
CC       specific displays a total absence of the posterior part of the
CC       anterior commissure and aberrant axon trajectories appearing in
CC       the external capsule; ventral telencephalon neuron-specific shows
CC       corticothalamic, thalamocortical and corticospinal tracts defect
CC       to various extent; telencephalon neuron-specific exhibits the full
CC       spectrum of axon defects seen in the classical null mutant
CC       knockout mice; cholinergic neuron-specific shows an absence of
CC       cholinergic fiber tracts passing through the striatum, a defective
CC       caudal migration of neurons of the VIIth motor nucleus and a loss
CC       of motor innervation to the face, a decrease in motor innervation
CC       of the tongue by the XIIth nerve and a complete loss of
CC       cholinergic neurons in the vomeronasal organ; oligodendrocyte
CC       neuron-specific leads to the complete spectrum of motor neuron
CC       phenotypes shown by the classical mutant knockout mice; caudal and
CC       upper thorax region-specific leads to a loss of motor innervation
CC       and an atrophy of anterior compartment muscles in the lower
CC       hindlimb by the deep peroneal nerve and a nearly absence in
CC       ascending spinal sensory axons in the brainstem, midbrain and
CC       thalamus altering the ability to transmit sensory information from
CC       the trunk and limbs to the brain in postnatal life
CC       (PubMed:24347548, PubMed:24799694). {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12351730,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:14671310, ECO:0000269|PubMed:16495441,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:21325504, ECO:0000269|PubMed:24347548,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:24799694}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Component of the Wnt-Fzd-
CC       LRP5-LRP6 complex that triggers beta-catenin signaling through
CC       inducing aggregation of receptor-ligand complexes into ribosome-
CC       sized signalsomes (By similarity). The beta-catenin canonical
CC       signaling pathway leads to the activation of disheveled proteins,
CC       inhibition of GSK-3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin
CC       and activation of Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway
CC       involving PKC and calcium fluxes has been seen for some family
CC       members, but it is not yet clear if it represents a distinct
CC       pathway or if it can be integrated in the canonical pathway, as
CC       PKC seems to be required for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3
CC       kinase. Both pathways seem to involve interactions with G-
CC       proteins. May be involved in transduction and intercellular
CC       transmission of polarity information during tissue morphogenesis
CC       and/or in differentiated tissues. Coreceptor along with RYK of Wnt
CC       proteins, such as WNT1. {ECO:0000250, ECO:0000269|PubMed:10097073,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:10395542, ECO:0000269|PubMed:15454084,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:16543246}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Component of a Wnt-signaling complex that contains a WNT
CC       protein, a FZD protein and LRP5 or LRP6. Interacts directly with
CC       LRP5 or LRP6; the interaction is promoted by Wnt-binding and
CC       signaling and inhibited by DKK1 (By similarity). Interacts (via
CC       the PDZ-binding motif) with GPOC (via its PDZ domain). Interacts
CC       with RSPO1 and RSPO3. {ECO:0000250, ECO:0000269|PubMed:11520064,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:16543246, ECO:0000269|PubMed:22653731}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       Q8BH60:Gopc; NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-6171689, EBI-296357;
CC       O75581:LRP6 (xeno); NbExp=4; IntAct=EBI-6171689, EBI-910915;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein. Golgi
CC       apparatus. Cell membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC       Note=Colocalizes with GOPC at the Golgi apparatus.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in chondrocytes.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Lys-Thr-X-X-X-Trp motif interacts with the PDZ domain of
CC       Dvl (Disheveled) family members and is involved in the activation
CC       of the Wnt/beta-catenin signaling pathway. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The FZ domain is involved in binding with Wnt ligands.
CC   -!- PTM: Ubiquitinated by ZNRF3, leading to its degradation by the
CC       proteasome. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

RP   INTERACTION WITH GOPC, AND SUBCELLULAR LOCATION.
RX   PubMed=11520064; DOI=10.1006/bbrc.2001.5430;
RA   Yao R., Maeda T., Takada S., Noda T.;
RT   "Identification of a PDZ domain containing Golgi protein, GOPC, as an
RT   interaction partner of frizzled.";
RL   Biochem. Biophys. Res. Commun. 286:771-778(2001).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway, which
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. May be involved in
CC       transduction and intercellular transmission of polarity
CC       information during tissue morphogenesis and/or in differentiated
CC       tissues. Plays a role in yolk sac angiogenesis and in placental
CC       vascularization. Binds to Wnt2, Wnt10B, Wnt5A, but not to Wnt2B or
CC       Wnt4.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Component of the Wnt-Fzd-
CC       LRP5-LRP6 complex that triggers beta-catenin signaling through
CC       inducing aggregation of receptor-ligand complexes into ribosome-
CC       sized signalosomes. The beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. May be involved in
CC       transduction and intercellular transmission of polarity
CC       information during tissue morphogenesis and/or in differentiated
CC       tissues. Coreceptor along with RYK of Wnt proteins, such as WNT1.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11448771}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Component of a Wnt-signaling complex that contains a WNT
CC       protein, a FZD protein and LRP5 or LRP6. Interacts directly with
CC       LRP5 or LRP6; the interaction is promoted by Wnt-binding and
CC       signaling and inhibited by DKK1. Interacts with GPOC, RSPO1 and
CC       RSPO3 (By similarity). {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       P98086:C1qa (xeno); NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-6254212, EBI-299840;
CC       P56704:WNT3A; NbExp=2; IntAct=EBI-6254212, EBI-6173037;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein. Golgi
CC       apparatus {ECO:0000250}. Cell membrane {ECO:0000250}; Multi-pass
CC       membrane protein {ECO:0000250}. Note=Colocalizes with GOPC at the
CC       Golgi apparatus. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Most abundant in fetal kidney, followed by
CC       brain and lung. In adult tissues, expressed in kidney, heart,
CC       pancreas and skeletal muscle.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The PDZ-binding motif mediates interaction with GOPC.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Lys-Thr-X-X-X-Trp motif interacts with the PDZ domain of
CC       Dvl (Disheveled) family members and is involved in the activation
CC       of the Wnt/beta-catenin signaling pathway. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The FZ domain is involved in binding with Wnt ligands.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- PTM: Ubiquitinated by ZNRF3, leading to its degradation by the
CC       proteasome. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:22575959}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

RP   NUCLEOTIDE SEQUENCE [MRNA] OF 100-217.
RC   TISSUE=Limb bud;
RX   PubMed=10512196;
RA   Nohno T., Kawakami Y., Wada N., Komaguchi C., Nishimatsu S.;
RT   "Differential expression of the frizzled family involved in Wnt
RT   signaling during chick limb development.";
RL   Cell. Mol. Biol. 45:653-659(1999).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway, which
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. May be involved in
CC       transduction and intercellular transmission of polarity
CC       information during tissue morphogenesis and/or in differentiated
CC       tissues.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein. Cell
CC       membrane {ECO:0000250}; Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: Expressed in prechordal plate between stages
CC       3 and 15.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The FZ domain is involved in binding with Wnt ligands.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway, which
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. May be involved in
CC       transduction and intercellular transmission of polarity
CC       information during tissue morphogenesis and/or in differentiated
CC       tissues. Required to coordinate the cytoskeletons of epidermal
CC       cells to produce a parallel array of cuticular hairs and bristles.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane {ECO:0000305}; Multi-pass membrane
CC       protein {ECO:0000305}.

CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway, which
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. Activation by Wnt5A
CC       stimulates PKC activity via a G-protein-dependent mechanism.
CC       Involved in transduction and intercellular transmission of
CC       polarity information during tissue morphogenesis and/or in
CC       differentiated tissues. Together with FZD3, may be involved in the
CC       neural tube closure and plays a role in the regulation of the
CC       establishment of planar cell polarity (PCP), particularly in the
CC       orientation of asymmetric bundles of stereocilia on the apical
CC       faces of a subset of auditory and vestibular sensory cells located
CC       in the inner ear (By similarity). {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q61089}.

RA   Nohno T., Kawakami Y., Wada N., Komaguchi C., Nishimatsu S.;

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway, which
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. May be involved in
CC       transduction and intercellular transmission of polarity
CC       information during tissue morphogenesis and/or in differentiated
CC       tissues. Plays a role in controlling early axon growth and
CC       guidance processes necessary for the formation of a subset of
CC       central and peripheral major fiber tracts. Involved in the
CC       migration of cranial neural crest cells. May also be implicated in
CC       the transmission of sensory information from the trunk and limbs
CC       to the brain. Controls commissural sensory axons guidance after
CC       midline crossing along the anterior-posterior axis in the
CC       developing spinal cord in a Wnt-dependent signaling pathway.
CC       Together with FZD6, is involved in the neural tube closure and
CC       plays a role in the regulation of the establishment of planar cell
CC       polarity (PCP). Promotes neurogenesis by maintaining sympathetic
CC       neuroblasts within the cell cycle in a beta-catenin-dependent
CC       manner (By similarity). {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q61086}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein. Cell
CC       membrane {ECO:0000250}; Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000250}.
CC       Cell surface {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q61086}. Apical cell membrane
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q61086}; Multi-pass membrane protein
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The FZ domain is involved in binding with Wnt ligands.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

RP   COUPLING TO BETA-CATENIN PATHWAY.
RX   PubMed=11142678; DOI=10.1046/j.1440-169x.2000.00545.x;
RA   Kawakami Y., Wada N., Nishimatsu S., Nohno T.;
RT   "Involvement of frizzled-10 in Wnt-7a signaling during chick limb
RT   development.";
RL   Dev. Growth Differ. 42:561-569(2000).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway, which
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. May be involved in
CC       transduction and intercellular transmission of polarity
CC       information during tissue morphogenesis and/or in differentiated
CC       tissues. Activation by Wnt7A induces expression of beta-catenin
CC       target genes.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane {ECO:0000305}; Multi-pass
CC       membrane protein {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed in the dorsal ectoderm overlying the
CC       developing spinal cord.
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: Expressed in the region posterior to the
CC       Hensen node at stage 6. Detected in the dorsal domain of the
CC       neural tube and the CNS of the developing embryo. In the
CC       developing limb, expression starts at stage 18 in the posterior-
CC       dorsal region of the distal mesenchyme, and gradually expands to
CC       the anterior-distal region. Also found in the feather bud and
CC       branchial arch.
CC   -!- INDUCTION: By Sonic hedgehog (Shh) in limb bud.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Lys-Thr-X-X-X-Trp motif interacts with the PDZ domain of
CC       Dvl (Disheveled) family members and is involved in the activation
CC       of the Wnt/beta-catenin signaling pathway. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The FZ domain is involved in binding with Wnt ligands.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

RP   FUNCTION.
RX   PubMed=24391920; DOI=10.1371/journal.pone.0084232;

RP   DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE, FUNCTION, AND SUBCELLULAR LOCATION.
RX   PubMed=24860427; DOI=10.3389/fncel.2014.00110;
RA   Aviles E.C., Pinto C., Hanna P., Ojeda J., Perez V., De Ferrari G.V.,
RA   Zamorano P., Albistur M., Sandoval D., Henriquez J.P.;
RT   "Frizzled-9 impairs acetylcholine receptor clustering in skeletal
RT   muscle cells.";
RL   Front. Cell. Neurosci. 8:110-110(2014).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for WNT2 that is coupled to the beta-catenin
CC       canonical signaling pathway, which leads to the activation of
CC       disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-3 kinase, nuclear
CC       accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of Wnt target genes
CC       (By similarity). Plays a role in neuromuscular junction (NMJ)
CC       assembly by negatively regulating the clustering of acetylcholine
CC       receptors (AChR) through the beta-catenin canonical signaling
CC       pathway (PubMed:24860427). May play a role in neural progenitor
CC       cells (NPCs) viability through the beta-catenin canonical
CC       signaling pathway by negatively regulating cell cycle arrest
CC       leading to inhibition of neuron apoptotic process (By similarity).
CC       During hippocampal development, regulates neuroblast proliferation
CC       and apoptotic cell death (PubMed:15930120). Controls bone
CC       formation through non canonical Wnt signaling mediated via ISG15
CC       (PubMed:21402791). Positively regulates bone regeneration through
CC       non canonical Wnt signaling (PubMed:24391920).
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:O00144, ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q8K4C8,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:15930120, ECO:0000269|PubMed:21402791,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:24391920, ECO:0000269|PubMed:24860427}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:24860427};
CC       Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000255}. Note=Relocalizes DVL1
CC       to the cell membrane leading to phosphorylation of DVL1 and AXIN1
CC       relocalization to the cell membrane.
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q8K4C8}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: In the embryo, found in the neural tube, trunk
CC       skeletal muscle precursors (myotomes), limb skeletal anlagen,
CC       craniofacial regions and nephric ducts. In the adult, expression
CC       is abundant in heart, brain, testis and skeletal muscle. In the
CC       testis, expressed in all spermatogenic cell types. Lower levels in
CC       adult lung, liver and kidney. Barely detectable in spleen.
CC       Expressed also in chondrocytes.
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: Not detected at embryonic day 7 (E7), weakly
CC       at E11 and strongly at E15 and E17. Expression covers the entire
CC       neural tube at 9.5 dpc, decreases at 10.5 dpc and becomes
CC       detectable only in the lumbar to tail regions at 11.5 dpc. In the
CC       somites, expression begins at 10.5 dpc to become up-regulated all
CC       along the rostrocaudal trunk axis at 11.5 dpc. In craniofacial
CC       territories, expression is first detected at 11.5 dpc in
CC       restricted areas of the nose, the maxillar mandibular and second
CC       branchial arch anlagen. At 11.5 dpc, predominantly expressed in
CC       restricted areas of the nose, dorsally to the eye and in the
CC       caudal pharyngeal region. Highly expressed at early stages of
CC       neuromuscular junction assembly (E14.5) and gradually decreases as
CC       development proceeds, being more than about 4-fold less expressed
CC       in E19.5. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10198163}.
CC   -!- INDUCTION: Increases during the initial stages of osteoblast
CC       differentiation. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:21402791}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Lys-Thr-X-X-X-Trp motif interacts with the PDZ domain of
CC       Dvl (Disheveled) family members and is involved in the activation
CC       of the Wnt/beta-catenin signaling pathway. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The FZ domain is involved in binding with Wnt ligands.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- PTM: Ubiquitinated by ZNRF3, leading to its degradation by the
CC       proteasome. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE: Homozygous Fzd9 knockout mice show deficits
CC       in spatial memory behaviors. Heterozygous and homozygous Fzd9
CC       knockout mice appear healthy, develop normally, and are fertile
CC       (PubMed:15930120). Homozygous Fzd9 knockout mice display
CC       osteopenia (PubMed:21402791). {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15930120,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:21402791}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- CAUTION: Has been first described as FZD3 in literature.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

RP   VARIANTS RETINOPATHY OF PREMATURITY ASN-203 AND GLY-370.
RX   PubMed=20141357; DOI=10.3109/13816810903479834;
RA   Ells A., Guernsey D.L., Wallace K., Zheng B., Vincer M., Allen A.,

RT   "Severe retinopathy of prematurity associated with FZD4 mutations.";
RL   Ophthalmic Genet. 31:37-43(2010).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin (CTNNB1) canonical signaling
CC       pathway, which leads to the activation of disheveled proteins,
CC       inhibition of GSK-3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin
CC       (CTNNB1) and activation of Wnt target genes. Plays a critical role
CC       in retinal vascularization by acting as a receptor for Wnt
CC       proteins and norrin (NDP). In retina, it can be both activated by
CC       Wnt protein-binding, but also by a Wnt-independent signaling via
CC       binding of norrin (NDP), promoting in both cases beta-catenin
CC       (CTNNB1) accumulation and stimulation of LEF/TCF-mediated
CC       transcriptional programs. A second signaling pathway involving PKC
CC       and calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it
CC       is not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can
CC       be integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be
CC       required for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both
CC       pathways seem to involve interactions with G-proteins. May be
CC       involved in transduction and intercellular transmission of
CC       polarity information during tissue morphogenesis and/or in
CC       differentiated tissues.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Interacts with MAGI3 and norrin (NDP). Component of a
CC       complex, at least composed of TSPAN12, FZD4 and norrin (NDP) (By
CC       similarity). {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       G3GTH2:I79_000956 (xeno); NbExp=2; IntAct=EBI-2466380, EBI-3504975;
CC       Q00604:NDP; NbExp=4; IntAct=EBI-2466380, EBI-2466352;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein. Cell
CC       membrane {ECO:0000250}; Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Almost ubiquitous. Largely expressed in adult
CC       heart, skeletal muscle, ovary, and fetal kidney. Moderate amounts
CC       in adult liver, kidney, pancreas, spleen, and fetal lung, and
CC       small amounts in placenta, adult lung, prostate, testis, colon,
CC       fetal brain and liver.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Lys-Thr-X-X-X-Trp motif interacts with the PDZ domain of
CC       Dvl (Disheveled) family members and is involved in the activation
CC       of the Wnt/beta-catenin signaling pathway. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The FZ domain is involved in binding with Wnt ligands.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- PTM: Ubiquitinated by ZNRF3, leading to its degradation by the
CC       proteasome. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:22575959}.
CC   -!- DISEASE: Vitreoretinopathy, exudative 1 (EVR1) [MIM:133780]: A
CC       disorder of the retinal vasculature characterized by an abrupt
CC       cessation of growth of peripheral capillaries, leading to an
CC       avascular peripheral retina. This may lead to compensatory retinal
CC       neovascularization, which is thought to be induced by hypoxia from
CC       the initial avascular insult. New vessels are prone to leakage and
CC       rupture causing exudates and bleeding, followed by scarring,
CC       retinal detachment and blindness. Clinical features can be highly
CC       variable, even within the same family. Patients with mild forms of
CC       the disease are asymptomatic, and their only disease related
CC       abnormality is an arc of avascular retina in the extreme temporal
CC       periphery. In many ways the disease resembles retinopathy of
CC       prematurity but there is no evidence of prematurity or small birth
CC       weight in the patient history. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12172548,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:14507768, ECO:0000269|PubMed:15035989,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:15223780, ECO:0000269|PubMed:15370539,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:15488808, ECO:0000269|PubMed:15733276,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:15981244, ECO:0000269|PubMed:17093393,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:17955262, ECO:0000269|PubMed:19172507,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:19324841, ECO:0000269|PubMed:20340138}.
CC       Note=The disease is caused by mutations affecting the gene
CC       represented in this entry.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

RP   NUCLEOTIDE SEQUENCE [MRNA] OF 265-325.
RC   TISSUE=Esophageal carcinoma;
RX   PubMed=9707618; DOI=10.1073/pnas.95.17.10164;
RA   Tanaka S., Akiyoshi T., Mori M., Wands J.R., Sugimachi K.;

RN   [4]
RP   INTERACTION WITH MYOC.
RX   PubMed=19188438; DOI=10.1128/MCB.01274-08;
RA   Kwon H.S., Lee H.S., Ji Y., Rubin J.S., Tomarev S.I.;
RT   "Myocilin is a modulator of Wnt signaling.";
RL   Mol. Cell. Biol. 29:2139-2154(2009).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway, which
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. May be involved in
CC       transduction and intercellular transmission of polarity
CC       information during tissue morphogenesis and/or in differentiated
CC       tissues.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Interacts with MYOC. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:19188438}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       A8MQ03:CYSRT1; NbExp=4; IntAct=EBI-8803802, EBI-3867333;
CC       Q9Y5L2:HILPDA; NbExp=2; IntAct=EBI-8803802, EBI-8803836;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane {ECO:0000250}; Multi-pass
CC       membrane protein {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Highest levels in the placenta and fetal
CC       kidney, followed by fetal lung and brain. In adult brain,
CC       abundantly expressed in the cerebellum, followed by cerebral
CC       cortex, medulla and spinal cord; very low levels in total brain,
CC       frontal lobe, temporal lobe and putamen. Weak expression detected
CC       in adult brain, heart, lung, skeletal muscle, pancreas, spleen and
CC       prostate.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Lys-Thr-X-X-X-Trp motif interacts with the PDZ domain of
CC       Dvl (Disheveled) family members and is involved in the activation
CC       of the Wnt/beta-catenin signaling pathway. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The FZ domain is involved in binding with Wnt ligands.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- PTM: Ubiquitinated by ZNRF3, leading to its degradation by the
CC       proteasome. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

RP   NUCLEOTIDE SEQUENCE [LARGE SCALE MRNA].
RC   STRAIN=Berkeley; TISSUE=Embryo;
RA   Stapleton M., Carlson J.W., Chavez C., Frise E., George R.A.,
RA   Pacleb J.M., Park S., Wan K.H., Yu C., Celniker S.E.;
RL   Submitted (JUN-2006) to the EMBL/GenBank/DDBJ databases.
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Receptor for Wnt proteins. Most of frizzled receptors
CC       are coupled to the beta-catenin canonical signaling pathway, which
CC       leads to the activation of disheveled proteins, inhibition of GSK-
CC       3 kinase, nuclear accumulation of beta-catenin and activation of
CC       Wnt target genes. A second signaling pathway involving PKC and
CC       calcium fluxes has been seen for some family members, but it is
CC       not yet clear if it represents a distinct pathway or if it can be
CC       integrated in the canonical pathway, as PKC seems to be required
CC       for Wnt-mediated inactivation of GSK-3 kinase. Both pathways seem
CC       to involve interactions with G-proteins. Required to coordinate
CC       the cytoskeletons of epidermal cells to produce a parallel array
CC       of cuticular hairs and bristles. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10097073}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       Q9W450:Grip; NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-118222, EBI-149374;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10097073};
CC       Multi-pass membrane protein {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10097073}.
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: Expression starts at stage 6 in all cells
CC       between 15 and 70 per cent of egg length, including the
CC       invaginating cells of the ventral furrow. Stripe pattern is
CC       emerging by early stage 8. From stage 9 and continuing throughout
CC       embryogenesis, expression is seen in the developing CNS. At stage
CC       10, expressed in 15 stripes in the presumptive head and trunk
CC       regions, in the posterior midgut primordium, in a subset of cells
CC       of anterior midgut invagination and in the procephalic lobe. At
CC       stage 12, expression declines in epidermis and increases in the
CC       midgut and visceral mesoderm. At stage 17, only expressed in the
CC       CNS, hindgut and dorsal vessel.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: Lys-Thr-X-X-X-Trp motif interacts with the PDZ domain of
CC       Dvl (Disheveled) family members and is involved in the activation
CC       of the Wnt/beta-catenin signaling pathway. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The FZ domain is involved in binding with Wnt ligands.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:8717036}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the G-protein coupled receptor Fz/Smo
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.
